From pdiaz-go at cameron.edu  Fri Jun 13 15:18:48 2014
From: pdiaz-go at cameron.edu (Pedro Diaz-Gomez)
Date: Fri, 13 Jun 2014 15:18:48 +0000
Subject: [Cs] Job posting at the Computing & Technology Department - Cameron
 University.
Message-ID: <30D8947C8344054F8F54654B508CC49659B42CB9@EXDB2.cameron.edu>

Good morning,

Y was wondering if it will be possible to post this posting/link regarding an opening in the Computing & Technology Department at Cameron University.
Assistant Professor/Instructor, Computing & Technology
Tracking Code
F1243M
Job Description

POSTED JOB TITLE: Assistant Professor/Instructor, Computer Science

JOB DESCRIPTION:  The Department of Computing and Technology at Cameron University invites applications for a fulltime regular faculty position beginning in August 2014.  This position primarily provides support for programs in the B.S. in Computer Science and the B.S. in Information Technology programs, potentially to include courses delivered to support university computer competency requirements.  With appropriate qualifications the faculty member in this position may also have the opportunity to contribute to the B.S. in Multimedia Design program.  The department seeks to fill this position at the rank of Assistant Professor (tenure-track) but will consider qualified individuals for the rank of Instructor (permanent, non-tenure track).  Applicants at the rank of Instructor must possess at least a master's degree in Information Technology, Computer Science, Computer Engineering, or a closely related field. Applicants at the rank of Assistant Professor must have an earned doctorate in Information Technology, Computer Science, Computer Engineering, or a closely related field.  Applications will be accepted from individuals who are nearing completion of their doctorate and expect to complete the degree within one calendar year (initial appointment would be at the rank and salary of Instructor with conversion to the rank and salary of Assistant Professor upon confirmation of degree completion).  Applicants with experience in Computer Game Development or Immersive Simulations will receive preferential consideration.  The person chosen for this appointment will be joining a department that includes twelve fulltime faculty members.
 Job duties include but are not limited to:
*     12 faculty load hour per semester teaching assignment, active participation in program assessment and in departmental recruitment and retention activities, and advising and mentoring undergraduate students.
*     Tenure-track faculty members are evaluated annually in the areas of teaching effectiveness, service, and scholarship.
*     Faculty members are highly encouraged to develop activities that support undergraduate research.
*     More information about the department and its program offerings is available online at: http://www.cameron.edu/comptech.
*     Additional information about faculty duties and evaluation is available online at: http://www.cameron.edu/fachandbook
 SUPERVISION: This position will report to the chairperson of the Department of Computing and Technology.
 MINIMUM QUALIFICATIONS:
1.  Applicants must possess a minimum of a master's degree from a regionally accredited university in Information Technology, Computer Science, Computer Engineering, or another closely related field
 PREFERRED QUALIFICATIONS:
1.  Applicants will possess an earned doctorate from a regionally accredited university in Information Technology, Computer Science, Computer Engineering, or another closely related field.
2.  Applicants with previous industry experience or demonstrated expertise in Computer Game Development or Immersive Simulations will receive preference.
3.             Demonstrated excellence in teaching at the undergraduate level is highly desired.
SALARY RANGE: Commensurate with education and experience.
INSTITUTION: Cameron University (www.cameron.edu) is a state-supported regional institution located in Lawton, Oklahoma, that offers undergraduate and graduate degrees. Dedicated to excellence, the university provides a wide range of economic, cultural, and educational opportunities for the betterment of all citizens. Master's-level graduate degrees are offered in business, behavioral sciences, and education; baccalaureate programs are offered in more than forty disciplines, and associate degrees are offered in many other studies. The close proximity of Fort Sill contributes to an area rich in cultural diversity and provides the opportunity for frequent cooperative efforts. The combined community of Lawton/Fort Sill has a population of more than 100,000 and is located adjacent to the picturesque Wichita Mountains Wildlife Refuge. A copy of the University's Annual Security Report, listing crime statistics and university policies, is available by contacting the Office of Public Safety or by accessing the report online at www.cameron.edu/ops<http://www.cameron.edu/ops>.  A broad view of university statistics and student demographics, and telephone numbers of three professional references.
APPLYING: Attachments should include a cover letter indicating experience applicable to position, resume, transcripts (unofficial are acceptable at this point), names, addresses, and telephone numbers of three professional references.

DEADLINE: Applications will be accepted until the position is filled; however, only candidates whose applications are received by June 20, 2014 are assured of receiving full consideration.

JOB #-F1243M
Job Location
Lawton, Oklahoma, United States
Position Type
Full-Time/Regular


https://cameron-openhire.silkroad.com/epostings/index.cfm?fuseaction=app.jobinfo&jobid=401&company_id=16345&version=1&source=ONLINE&JobOwner=992282&startflag=1

Thanks in advance for your time.

Pedro A. Diaz Gomez, Ph.D.
Associate Professor - Computing & Technology Department
Cameron University - Lawton OK - (580)-581-7934 USA
Certified Information Systems Security Professional - CISSP
GIAC Certified Intrusion Analyst - GCIA

Subject: [Cs] Computer Science resources and career paths - quick question
Message-ID: <10212390277272363424298@Doug>

Hi there,

I'm hoping you can help me with a quick request. 

Our organization created a unique Computer Science career and post-secondary education guide tailored to the needs of current and future students, and those pursuing a career in Computer Science.  It includes industry resources, career paths, scholarships, supplemental free online courses, and internship opportunities.  What makes this unique for current and future college students is that we've consolidated actionable materials in one place - students can search professional organizations and career information and then apply for specific Computer Science scholarships and internships. 

Anyone can access our no-cost Computer Science guide here:

     http://www.affordablecollegesonline.org/online-colleges/computer-science-programs/

I noticed that you list Computer Science related resources including the Computer website on http://www.cs.ou.edu/~hougen/

Our mission is to get these free community education resources into the hands of students.  Do you think you could help by listing our Computer Science guide on your page mentioned above or on a similar resource listing page?

Thank you,

Dan Schuessler
Chief Affordability Officer
Affordable Colleges Foundation
650-209-8505

About Us:  Affordable Colleges Foundation came to be in 2011 with the mission to provide strategies and information about pursuing an affordable higher education.  Our free community resources materials and tools span topics such as financial-aid and college savings strategies, affordability and scorecard rankings, opportunities for Veterans and people with disabilities, and online learning resources.  We have been featured by nearly 500 top universities in the United States, Canada, and the UK along by several many state and local government organizations.

If you wish to unsubscribe from our mailing list, please click here: www.affordablecollegesonline.org/unsubscribe/

From rburdwel at tamusa.tamus.edu  Wed Nov 19 20:25:27 2014
From: rburdwel at tamusa.tamus.edu (Robert A. Burdwell)
Date: Wed, 19 Nov 2014 14:25:27 -0600
Subject: [Cs] Invitation to Compete in the 2015 Southwest Regional
 Collegiate Cyber Defense Competition
Message-ID: <51F163D6B47CDA4AB4E7984B34E3DCBD1DA37DE354@MAIL-STOREA.tamusa.tamus.edu>

Hello,

We would like to take this opportunity to extend an invitation for your school to participate in the Collegiate Cyber Defense Competition (CCDC) for 2015. The Southwest Region includes the states of Arkansas, Louisiana, Oklahoma, New Mexico, and Texas.  We are trying to contact computing sciences programs within those states to increase the participation in the Southwest Region.  Your school has not participated in previous CCDCs and may not be aware of the competition.  Each school may have one competitive team, composed of eight students (no more than 2 graduate students).  Because each school is limited to a single team we have tried to send this email to representatives from each department that might have an information assurance or computer security program.  If this mail was sent to you by mistake, then please forward it to the appropriate person in your department or school.  If there is another department at your school listed in this email, you should coordinate with them, as only one team per school is allowed.

The CCDC is a defensive only computer security competition for college students.  A list of the teams is available at http://www.southwestccdc.org/.  This site also contains information about the national competition and links to websites that can assist a school that is just beginning their involvement in the competition.  Regional CCDCs are conducted early in the year (January to March) with the winners from each region competing in the National CCDC in April in San Antonio.  More information on the national competition can be found at http://nationalccdc.org/.

There is time for your school to consider whether it will participate or not in the coming year.  We intend to conduct the preliminary round of competition virtually, which saves on travel costs while allowing your teams to experience the activities of a CCDC event.  There is no expense associated with this preliminary competition and participation this year would give your school some idea of whether you might want to participate in future years.  Please review the information on our website and the National CCDC website, paying special attention to the information on the "Staring a 2015 team" link or click on the https://www.surveymonkey.com/s/2015SWCCDC registration link. You may also forward this to any schools in your area that may want to participate.

Please let us know if you want us to remove your name from the email list.  We will be sending out a registration reminders in the coming weeks. We ask that you register early if you plan to participate, as we will be using registration numbers to determine the schedule for the preliminary round of competitions.

Thanks,


Robert Burdwell, Ph.D., PMP
Microsoft Certified Professional
Adobe Certified Expert
Certified Ethical Hacker (CEH)
Titanium Certified App Developer (TCAD)

School of Business
Texas A&M University - San Antonio

From rburdwel at tamusa.tamus.edu  Tue Nov 25 16:42:34 2014
From: rburdwel at tamusa.tamus.edu (Robert A. Burdwell)
Date: Tue, 25 Nov 2014 10:42:34 -0600
Subject: [Cs] Invitation to Compete in the 2015 Southwest Regional
 Collegiate Cyber Defense Competition
Message-ID: <51F163D6B47CDA4AB4E7984B34E3DCBD1DA3ED62D2@MAIL-STOREA.tamusa.tamus.edu>

Hello,

We would like to take this opportunity to extend an invitation for your school to participate in the Collegiate Cyber Defense Competition (CCDC) for 2015. The Southwest Region includes the states of Arkansas, Louisiana, Oklahoma, New Mexico, and Texas.  We are trying to contact computing sciences programs within those states to increase the participation in the Southwest Region.  Your school has not participated in previous CCDCs and may not be aware of the competition.  Each school may have one competitive team, composed of eight students (no more than 2 graduate students).  Because each school is limited to a single team we have tried to send this email to representatives from each department that might have an information assurance or computer security program.  If this mail was sent to you by mistake, then please forward it to the appropriate person in your department or school.  If there is another department at your school listed in this email, you should coordinate with them, as only one team per school is allowed.

The CCDC is a defensive only computer security competition for college students.  A list of the teams is available at http://www.southwestccdc.org/.  This site also contains information about the national competition and links to websites that can assist a school that is just beginning their involvement in the competition.  Regional CCDCs are conducted early in the year (January to March) with the winners from each region competing in the National CCDC in April in San Antonio.  More information on the national competition can be found at http://nationalccdc.org/.

There is time for your school to consider whether it will participate or not in the coming year.  We intend to conduct the preliminary round of competition virtually, which saves on travel costs while allowing your teams to experience the activities of a CCDC event.  There is no expense associated with this preliminary competition and participation this year would give your school some idea of whether you might want to participate in future years.  Please review the information on our website and the National CCDC website, paying special attention to the information on the "Staring a 2015 team" link or clicking on the https://www.surveymonkey.com/s/2015SWCCDC registration link. You may also forward this to any schools in your area that may want to participate.

Please let us know if you want us to remove your name from the email list.  We will be sending out a registration reminders in the coming weeks. We ask that you register early if you plan to participate, as we will be using registration numbers to determine the schedule for the preliminary round of competitions.

Thanks,

From rburdwel at tamusa.tamus.edu  Wed Dec 10 18:18:44 2014
From: rburdwel at tamusa.tamus.edu (Robert A. Burdwell)
Date: Wed, 10 Dec 2014 12:18:44 -0600
Subject: [Cs] Invitation to Compete in the 2015 Southwest Regional
 Collegiate Cyber Defense Competition - Team Registration will close soon
Message-ID: <51F163D6B47CDA4AB4E7984B34E3DCBD1DA77DEC2E@MAIL-STOREA.tamusa.tamus.edu>

Team Registration will Close Soon

Hello,

We would like to take this opportunity to extend an invitation for your school to participate in the Collegiate Cyber Defense Competition (CCDC) for 2015. The Southwest Region includes the states of Arkansas, Louisiana, Oklahoma, New Mexico, and Texas.  We are trying to contact computing sciences programs within those states to increase the participation in the Southwest Region.  Your school has not participated in previous CCDCs and may not be aware of the competition.  Each school may have one competitive team, composed of eight students (no more than 2 graduate students).  Because each school is limited to a single team we have tried to send this email to representatives from each department that might have an information assurance or computer security program.  If this mail was sent to you by mistake, then please forward it to the appropriate person in your department or school.  If there is another department at your school listed in this email, you should coordinate with them, as only one team per school is allowed.

The CCDC is a defensive only computer security competition for college students.  A list of the teams is available at http://www.southwestccdc.org/.  This site also contains information about the national competition and links to websites that can assist a school that is just beginning their involvement in the competition.  Regional CCDCs are conducted early in the year (January to March) with the winners from each region competing in the National CCDC in April in San Antonio.  More information on the national competition can be found at http://nationalccdc.org/.

There is time for your school to consider whether it will participate or not in the coming year.  We intend to conduct the preliminary round of competition virtually, which saves on travel costs while allowing your teams to experience the activities of a CCDC event.  There is no expense associated with this preliminary competition and participation this year would give your school some idea of whether you might want to participate in future years.  Please review the information on our website and the National CCDC website, paying special attention to the information on the "Staring a 2015 team" link or clicking on the https://www.surveymonkey.com/s/2015SWCCDC registration link. You may also forward this to any schools in your area that may want to participate.

Please let us know if you want us to remove your name from the email list.  We will be sending out a registration reminders in the coming weeks. We ask that you register early if you plan to participate, as we will be using registration numbers to determine the schedule for the preliminary round of competitions.

Thanks,


Robert Burdwell, Ph.D., PMP
Microsoft Certified Professional
Adobe Certified Expert
Certified Ethical Hacker (CEH)
Titanium Certified App Developer (TCAD)

School of Business
Texas A&M University - San Antonio
Tel: 210-784-2308

The application deadline for the  2015 Secretary?s Honors Program Cyber Student Volunteer Initiative<https://www.usajobs.gov/GetJob/ViewDetails/386746100> has been extended to January 23, 2015, and interested students may apply via USAJOBS.gov<https://www.usajobs.gov/GetJob/ViewDetails/386746100>. Please feel free to share this flyer with your students who may wish to participate in this exciting opportunity. We?ve also included sample templates for sharing via email/Facebook and Twitter<https://www.twitter.com/DHSgov/status/536977267810123776> below for your convenience. All applications should be submitted at https://www.usajobs.gov/GetJob/ViewDetails/386746100. Best regards,

CyberSkills Management Support Initiative



Sample Email Blast

The Department of Homeland Security announced the launch of the 2015 Secretary's Honors Program Cyber Student Volunteer Initiative<https://www.usajobs.gov/GetJob/ViewDetails/386746100> for current two- and four-year college students. Beginning in the spring of 2015, more than 75 selected students will complete volunteer assignments supporting the DHS cyber mission at department field offices in over 50 locations across the country. Through this initiative, student volunteers currently pursuing an undergraduate degree related to cybersecurity will gain invaluable hands-on experience and exposure to the cybersecurity work performed across DHS. In addition to supporting activities such as cyber threat analysis, digital forensics, network diagnostics and incident response, selected students will participate in mentoring and professional development events with DHS managers and senior leaders.

Students interested in applying to the 2015 program may submit their applications through USAJOBS.gov<https://www.usajobs.gov/GetJob/ViewDetails/386746100>.

Hello!

My name is Sam Marino, and I am on the recruitment team for Relay for life here at OU.   I was hoping that your student organization would be interested in forming a team for our event this year!

Just in case you aren't familiar with Relay For Life, it is an international organization that raises money for the American Cancer Society.  All of the money we raise goes directly to cancer research and programs for cancer patients in our community, and across the nation.  Students are able to form teams and fundraise throughout the year to support this great cause.  The actual event will take place on Friday, April 24th in the South Oval.  The event is filled with games, performers, fun competitions and music throughout the night.  We will also spend time celebrating and remembering those who have been affected or are currently battling cancer.

OU's Relay For Life raised over $120,000 last year, and we would love for your organizations to help us reach our goal of $200,000 this year.  One of my main goals for this year is to get the entire OU campus involved in Relay For Life so that we can work together to better our community, and hopefully make cancer history.

To sign up go to www.ou.edu/rela<http://www.ou.edu/relay>y and sign up as a Team Captain.  Once you are signed up as a Team Captain the other members of your organization will be able to sign up on your team, and you can all begin fundraising!

I would love the opportunity to come to one of your organization's upcoming meetings to speak with your group more about Relay For Life, if this is something you might be willing to do please let me know! We are also having a team captain meeting on Monday, February 2nd at 8:30 in Zarrow Hall.  If you are considering creating a team, I greatly encourage you to attend this meeting so you can get more information about the event!

If you have any questions please don't hesitate to email me at Samuel.F.Marino-1 at ou.edu, or I would be more than happy to set up a meeting with you or any of your organization's officers to help you through the process.

Thank you for your time, and I hope to hear from you soon!

With Respect,

Sam Marino

From Kimberly at cse.tamu.edu  Fri Jan 30 17:37:03 2015
From: Kimberly at cse.tamu.edu (Kimberly Mallett)
Date: Fri, 30 Jan 2015 11:37:03 -0600
Subject: [Cs] NSF - REU at TEXAS A&M University - Computing for Disasters
Message-ID: <CADqcWOe3V2eRUyK6_8eTwbazTYqEHMJvFOu2OtjBjgOGr+p1bw@mail.gmail.com>

*Texas A&M University *
*NSF- Research Experience for Undergraduates (REU) program *
*Computing for Disasters*



*APPLICATION DEADLINE: March 1, 2015
<https://apply2.cse.tamu.edu/gts/applicant/reu/>  *

*PROGRAM DATES: June 2, 2015 ? August 7, 2015*


*PROGRAM INCLUDES:*

*  Hands-on research with responders

*  Seminars and brown bags on research & career development

*  Tours of TAMU laboratories & NASA Johnson

*  Weekly social activities with other students, mentors, & faculty


*AWARD:*

*  $5,000 for your research work for the summer

*  $1000 meal allowance

*  $1000 housing allowance (if not living in luxury housing provided)

*  Actual travel expenses to and from Texas A&M University


Summer 2015 will mark the third year that the Department of Computer
Science and Engineering at Texas A&M University is offering a summer REU
Program, Computing for Disasters. The program spans 10 weeks and involves
undergraduate students from Texas A&M as well as students from other
colleges and universities from across the United States. It is hoped that
the students participating in the CSE REU Computing for Disasters program
will make significant contributions to ongoing faculty research and, more
importantly, will gain an appreciation for and an interest in graduate
school and a future research career.

Disasters pose a comprehensive need for computing, where data must be
collected, transmitted, transformed, and displayed to stakeholders in
real-time, leading to the acronym of critical real-time computing and
information systems or CRICIS. Disasters are a natural focus because it
brings together research in "physical science and engineering (e.g.,
sensors, unmanned systems, models, etc.), social sources of data (e.g.,
social networking, citizen science, etc.), transfer and storage of data
(e.g., networks, cloud computing, context-aware networks, data warehousing,
security, privacy, etc.), transformation of data into useful information
(e.g., computer vision, human computation, etc.), real-time formal and
informal decision making support (e.g., artificial intelligence,
optimization, visualization, interfaces, cognitive science, CSCW, policy,
etc.)." However, disasters are more than a "big tent" offering a common
theme, they encourage expansion of existing research topics in new
directions because of the extreme temporal, geographical, stakeholder, and
data scales. In addition disaster management requires a new style of
research which emphasizes a holistic, multi-disciplinary approach similar
to the Smart Health and Well being programs at NSF.

Students are offered a specific project based on their interests and course
work as part of the acceptance process. They work with responders at
Disaster City in Week 1 and learn about human-centered design in computing,
then from week 2-9 work with their faculty and graduate mentors on
individual research projects. They also meet weekly as a cohort for brown
bag seminars on how to conduct research, career paths, and work/life
balance, and in week 10 present at two poster sessions. Students also tour
NASA Johnson Space Center and interact with industry and have lots of
social experiences.


*ELIGIBILITY:*

*  Undergraduate students majoring in computer science, computer
engineering, or related field

*  High school graduates who have been accepted at an undergraduate
institution but who have not yet started their undergraduate study are also
eligible to participate

*  U.S. Citizen or permanent resident

*  GPA of 3.0 or higher

*  Plan to graduate no earlier than December 2015

*  May not enroll in additional academic courses during the summer session

*  Minorities and women strongly encouraged to apply



Click here to apply or for more information.
<http://engineering.tamu.edu/cse/research/undergraduate-research/reu/computing-for-disasters>





*Kimberly Mallett*
Program Specialist I
Texas A&M University
Center for Robot-Assisted Search and Rescue (CRASAR)
Center for Emergency Informatics/EDGE Innovation Center
Department of Computer Science and Engineering

Girls Who Code Is Hiring Paid Teaching Staff
Gearing up for a drastically expanded 2015 Summer Immersion Program, national non-profit
Girls Who Code is looking to triple its teaching staff across the country! The organization
encourages empathetic and enthusiastic women and men with technical backgrounds 
to APPLY NOW for hundreds of available paid Teacher and Teaching Assistant positions:
girlswhocode.com/get-involved [http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?f=001oCPF0Cba3CaYg5edub0JxE94e8VW8mnhF-94WTbNeu0fWAHaL6McA-vCyuXG9MPbUMXzFZQ8E0wMGNgLSeCyItEEiqg6TIVTSdEuBXeuvG_ysm0HTbkbonXwqi0bnW_K89q8ZGi68EdzXAK2W-EeObmbx6ofhEsH7mlvkQi_NeE2NdTzQ8wOHjKFkOIgEEZR&c=-Y0flepzLqX8L749bKUFd43QJXXQAeSr2yGKxlFvLfMkJKwACv72Rw==&ch=BnVJ8wdCGOlpE4h6ID4bMnI4xySBRs4LY0N9TQe-U2mWVnsbklqOuQ==]
In the 7-week Summer Immersion Program, Girls Who Code embeds classrooms of 20 girls
each in technology companies and universities across the country to create a fun,
collaborative environment for girls to learn to code while becoming immersed in 
the technology industry.
The Girls Who Code teaching staff -- working in teams of 1 Teacher and 2 Teaching
Assistants per program -- defines the classroom experience and is the foundation
 of the organization's success in equipping girls to pursue computer science.
Teaching at Girls Who Code offers individuals the unique opportunity to empower 
teenage girls with computing skills to change the world while sharpening their own
tech skills and making lasting industry connections. Teaching staff will get the
 opportunity to work at one of the following companies:
Accenture, Adobe, AIG, Akamai, AOL Charitable Foundation, AppNexus, AT&T, BSA | 
The Software Alliance, eBay, Electronic Arts, Expedia, Facebook, GE, Goldman Sachs,
Google, Groupon, IAC, IBM, Intel, Intuit, Lockheed Martin, MassMutual, Microsoft,
Moody's, Pixar Animation Studios, Square, The Honest Company, Twitter, Viacom, and
Verizon.
For questions, please contact:
Emily Reid
Curriculum Director, Girls Who Code
emilyr at girlswhocode.com [mailto:emilyr at girlswhocode.com]

From amy.cole at researchandmarkets.org  Fri Feb  6 17:46:12 2015
From: amy.cole at researchandmarkets.org (Amy Cole)
Date: Fri, 6 Feb 2015 17:46:12 +0000
Subject: [Cs] =?utf-8?q?Algebraic_and_Discrete_Mathematical_Methods_for_Mo?=
	=?utf-8?q?dern_Biology?=
Message-ID: <6f2d943b-9842-4a5a-9742-4ef68d462055@it-falcon.exch2010-forward.nor.ouint>

Written by expert authors in both mathematics and biology, Algebraic and Discrete Mathematical Methods for Modern Biology offers a bridge between math and biology and provides a framework for simulating, analyzing, predicting, and modulating the behavior of complex biological systems. Each chapter begins with a question from modern biology, followed by the description of certain mathematical methods and theory appropriate in the search of answers.   

Every topic gives readers a fast-track pathway through the problem by presenting the biological foundation, covering the relevant mathematical theory, and highlighting connections between them. Multiple exercises and projects are embedded in each chapter. Many of the projects and exercises utilize specialized software, providing students with much-needed familiarity and experience with computing applications, critical components of the "modern biology" skill set.   

Algebraic and Discrete Mathematical Methods for Modern Biology is appropriate for mathematics courses such as finite mathematics, discrete structures, linear algebra, abstract/modern algebra, graph theory, probability, bioinformatics, statistics, biostatistics, and modeling, as well as for biology courses such as genetics, cell and molecular biology, biochemistry, ecology, and evolution.   

- Examines significant questions in modern biology and their mathematical treatments   
- Presents important mathematical concepts, methods, and tools in the context of essential biology   
- Features material of interest to students in both mathematics and biology   
- Presents chapters in modular format so topics taught in class need not follow the Table of Contents   
- Provides students with many examples and exercises to enhance comprehension   
- Introduces projects appropriate for undergraduate research   
- Utilizes freely accessible specialized software for visualization, simulation, and analysis in modern biology   
- Employs concepts from modern discrete mathematics and abstract algebra, which do not require calculus as a prerequisite   

For more information please click on:   
http://www.researchandmarkets.com/publication/mw9axp8/algebraic_and_discrete_mathematical_methods_f   

Title Index:   

Preface   
1. Graph Theory for Systems Biology: Interval graphs, motifs, and patterns recognition   
2. Food Webs and Graphs   
3. Adaptation: Discrete and algebraic approaches   
4. Signaling Networks: Asynchronous Boolean models   
5. Dymanics Over Complex Boolean Networks: Canalization, stability, and criticality   
6. Steady State Analysis of Boolean Models: A dimension reduction approach   
7. BioModel Engineering: Using Petri nets   
8. Transmission of Infectious Diseases: Data, models, and simulations   
9. Disease Transmission Dynamics on Networks: Network structure versus disease dynamics   
10. Predicting Correlated Responses in Quantitative Traits Under Selection: A linear algebra approach   
11. Metabolome Analysis: Modern algebraic and geometric methods   
12. Reconstructing the Phylogeny: Computational methods   
13. RNA Secondary Structures: Combinatorial approaches   
14. RNA Secondary Structures: An approach through pseudoknots and fatgraphs   

Authors:   

Robeva, Raina   

For more information please click on:   
http://www.researchandmarkets.com/publication/mw9axp8/algebraic_and_discrete_mathematical_methods_f   


Pricing:

Certificate in Computer Science Education at St. Scholastica

Scratch. App Inventor. Java.

Even though they sound like a team of superheroes from a comic book, these names
 represent some of the latest advancements in computer science education. And as
 a computer science teacher, you'll be expected to keep pace with all of them &#x2212;
even if you have no formal educational training on them.

We can change that.

With our Certificate in Computer Science Education [http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?f=001DIANiXOLKccDvTjmzNthaasEhFYvtydGey8QAYU0k85YkZiMtQE8Vj8QOynmgJD1udc5mI0dYxPewp96eAKZVPnzHIKqXGmMwa66lCYAxTCNbkGvB_2UxaoklmGb_T8lFKaSLsuB7iIbS9vkLquNYfQGagKVRtL53nsQfuDH1kHmBF6U9YGjL9Is4AtDXrlzQPjUQzhGAMu51cs_7X1bovxO28i15DwXto15Cp9i_UfauN-Rw2ZN9kucXA0_BIf1s96Fqj5cZyu9levRf8Ws60xwxKCLnd9DbtV4GUE6qWi6Q45IwDV5Yc1wCLqCmV-eBm9MP8wSrKRseKX1_auZxlgvXTB_85nY&c=DzLRLJtL62fyiZSzd1bR1U9tWGzs79BflDg1nr5yUWmwhYYkga64YA==&ch=6Ct2bD5DjbeYppSSxPAtaTvUhC-0SZwNddVQc6SgJRH1kpqxurq9Ag==],
you'll learn about the new technologies and teaching methods you'll need to take
 you and your students to the next level &#x2212; no matter if they're beginners,
advanced placement students or anywhere in between.

And with 100% online courses, an affordable tuition rate and a part-time format 
that allows you to complete the certificate in just over a year without interfering
with your home and work life, you can do it on your terms.

The credits earned through your Certificate in Computer Science Education can be
 applied toward our Master of Education program to meet elective strand requirements.

The next term starts on March 16. Apply by March 2 [http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?f=001DIANiXOLKccDvTjmzNthaasEhFYvtydGey8QAYU0k85YkZiMtQE8Vj8QOynmgJD1eEoyWK-uGdBLXe9OHwjiDvlTR5iqBUTIFxhRt-MD9FxR9JerJn6v7GU3sfndt_1KHkxZfT-93jnf2Y69cWY487BMI4HcZVKJwxtHl4Mq5_az47sTwfQytBUgC724cRNJVRx7F1cmEdc=&c=DzLRLJtL62fyiZSzd1bR1U9tWGzs79BflDg1nr5yUWmwhYYkga64YA==&ch=6Ct2bD5DjbeYppSSxPAtaTvUhC-0SZwNddVQc6SgJRH1kpqxurq9Ag==]
to secure your spot in the class.

Hi, just a reminder that you're receiving this email because you have expressed 
an interest in CSTA. Don't forget to add announcements at csta-hq.org to your address
book so we'll be sure to land in your inbox!
Call for Papers and Participation: WiPSCE 2015

We invite you to submit a paper, report, or poster for the 10th Workshop in Primary
and Secondary Computing Education (WiPSCE 2015) and join us in

London, United Kingdom, on November 9-11, 2015. WiPSCE aims at improving the exchange
of research and practice relevant to teaching and learning in primary and secondary
computing education, teacher training, and related research.

Important 2015 Dates

Submission deadline: Monday, June 1

Re-submission deadline: Monday, June 8

Notification of acceptance: Monday, July 27

Submission of revised manuscripts: Monday, September 15

Early Registration deadline: Monday, October 19

Original submissions in all areas related to primary and secondary computing education
are invited in the following categories:


* Full paper (6-10 pages): expected to meet one of two categories - empirical research
papers and philosophical research papers
* Work in progress (3-4 pages): unpublished original research in progress
* Practical report (4-6 pages): unpublished, original projects in the field of "primary
and secondary computing education"
* Posters (2 page abstract)
Topics include:

* Learning: attitudes, beliefs, motivation, misconceptions, learning difficulties,
student engagement with educational technology (e.g., visualization), conceptualization
of computing
* Teaching: teaching approaches, teaching methods, teaching with educational technology
* Content: curricular aspects, learning standards, tools, educational approaches,
context relevant teaching, assessment
* Institutional aspects: establishing and enhancing computing education, professional
development
Special Theme: Computing? How young is too young?
For more information, please contact:
Judith Gal-Ezer: galezer at cs.openu.ac.il [mailto:galezer at cs.openu.ac.il]
Sue Sentence: sue.sentance at kcl.ac.uk [mailto:sue.sentance at kcl.ac.uk]
Jan Vahrenhold: jan.vahrenhold at uni-muenster.de [mailto:jan.vahrenhold at uni-muenster.de]

From alkrauss48 at gmail.com  Mon Feb  9 20:42:01 2015
From: alkrauss48 at gmail.com (Aaron Krauss)
Date: Mon, 9 Feb 2015 14:42:01 -0600
Subject: [Cs] Speaking to Programming Classes
Message-ID: <etPan.54d91b99.38437fdb.128@aarons-mbp.local>

Hello,

Hello, my name is Aaron Krauss, and I?m a programmer in the Edmond / Oklahoma City area. I?m a 24 year old developer who?s been in the programming world for a while now, and I really enjoy speaking to students about the things that I wish I knew when I was in school studying programming.

I would love to know if any of the OU CS professors would be interested in having me speak to your students for a class (or half a class - I know you have busy class schedules) sometime this semester about what being a developer in the real world is like. I?ve given this talk a few times at other college classes and AP high school programming classes, and it usually ends up being 40ish minutes. The teachers have always told me that it?s valuable for the students to get an idea of what it?s like to be a developer, the things that I deal with, and the things they should be learning on their own in addition to what school is teaching them. It?s not so much teaching new material as it is showing them how massive the programming world is, and everything they could be doing.

I've really enjoyed giving these talks, and if you are interested, I?d certainly enjoy speaking to as many classes as you would deem beneficial. Here?s a PDF of my speaking outline:?

http://thesocietea.org/assets/documents/programming_speaking_outline.pdf

And you can take a look at my personal site if you?d like to learn more about me: http://thesocietea.org/

Thanks so much for your time, and feel free to ask me anything. This is all of my own free will, so definitely no payment or anything is expected; I just really enjoy speaking to and helping students.

Take care,

Aaron Krauss
Developer
thesocietea.org

P.S. I did graduate from OU?s MIS school in 2012 if that grants me any brownie points - though I chose to stay on the path of hardcore programming.

From icnc-fskd-cfp at hnu.edu.cn  Tue Feb 10 00:47:23 2015
From: icnc-fskd-cfp at hnu.edu.cn (Prof Li)
Date: Tue, 10 Feb 2015 08:47:23 +0800
Subject: [Cs] ICNC-FSKD 2015 Submissions due 10 February: Submitting to IEEE
	Xplore/EI Compendex/ISI 2015/2/10 8:47:34 z54nd
Message-ID: <20150210084734326216@hnu.edu.cn>

Dear Colleague,
 
We cordially invite you to submit a paper to the upcoming 2015 11th International Conference on Natural Computation (ICNC 2015) and 2015 12th International Conference on Fuzzy Systems and Knowledge Discovery (FSKD 2015), to be jointly held from 15-17 August 2015 in Zhangjiajie, China. 
 
Zhangjiajie is a city in the northwestern part of Hunan province. Nearby is the Wulingyuan Scenic Area, a UNESCO World Heritage Site and an AAAAA (the highest class) scenic area in China. Towering sandstones mesas, dense forests, and deep ravines form the gorgeous and mysterious natural landscape. With many spectacularly-shaped stone pillars, hidden valleys, seas of cloud, majestic waterfalls, wandering streams, clear lakes, and limestone caves, Wulingyuan is a must-see in China. Avatar, James Cameron?s block-buster movie, did much of its filming in these beautiful mountains.  
 
As with the past ICNC-FSKD conferences, all papers in conference proceedings will be submitted to both EI Compendex and ISTP (ISI Proceedings), as well as IEEE Xplore (all previous ICNC-FSKD conferences from 2005 to 2013 have been indexed in Ei Compendex). Extended versions of selected best papers will appear in an ICNC-FSKD special issue of International Journal on Pattern Recognition and Artificial Intelligence, a SCI-index journal. ICNC-FSKD 2015 is technically co-sponsored by the IEEE Circuits and Systems Society (pending).
 
ICNC-FSKD is a premier international forum for scientists and researchers to present the state of the art of data mining and intelligent methods inspired from nature, particularly biological, linguistic, and physical systems, with applications to computers, circuits, systems, control, robotics, communications, and more. This is an exciting and emerging interdisciplinary area in which a wide range of theory and methodologies are being investigated and developed to tackle complex and challenging problems. The registration fee of US-D410 includes proceedings, lunches, dinners, banquet, coffee breaks, and all technical sessions.
 
To promote international participation of researchers from outside the country/region where the conference is held (i.e., China?s mainland), researchers outside of China?s mainland are encouraged to propose invited sessions. An honorarium of US-D400 will be enjoyed by the organizer(s) for each completed (with at least 6 registered papers) invited session. The first author of each paper in an invited session must not be affiliated with an organization in China?s mainland. "(Invited Paper)" may be added below the title of each paper in the invited sessions. Invited session organizers will solicit submissions, conduct reviews and recommend accept/reject decisions on the submitted papers. Invited session organizers will be able to set their own submission and review schedules, as long as a set of recommended papers is determined by 3 June 2015. Each invited session proposal should include: (1) the name, bio, and contact information of each organizer of the invited session; (2) the title and a short synopsis of the invited session. Please send your proposal to icnc-fskd at hnu.edu.cn
 
For more information, visit the conference web page:
 
   http://icnc-fskd.hnu.edu.cn/
 
If you have any questions after visiting the conference web page, please email the secretariat at icnc-fskd at hnu.edu.cn
 
Join us at this major event in beautiful Zhangjiajie !!!
 
Organizing Committee
icnc-fskd at hnu.edu.cn
 
P.S.: Kindly forward to your colleagues and students in your school/department.
 
If you wish to unsubscribe, in which case we apologize, please reply with " unsubscribe  cs at ou.edu " in your email subject. Thanks.
 
 
2015/2/10 8:47:34 nzsdy2kfy

Leveraging MOOCs for CSP Professional Development

In 2014, the Mobile CSP [http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?f=001LhKKX9E9X13uh6TW2tG0eMh5D41CW2X2uo5F3IrKXAO53mebB-pcFpXhDRuhIiqAjgqOG5lqOIFeYXnVOVVCDDBfn9-ht4_osakfS9DMxcsqViqoQ1ARVeUMiSv6L5e25rCY7TtaV7s38P1uSZrgdGf_DWWNa6ErxH_f0LLHDlE=&c=KveG1NalNOS1hgPOq4HK2PI8xyPosyHPyLG1JyzVWrmYdcGWt4URgA==&ch=lAKMjbdjY9o5adQ_kg67es8JPwDVSis6jyxWz9J2dv-GNRFwP8ACnQ==]
and CSP4HS [http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?f=001LhKKX9E9X13uh6TW2tG0eMh5D41CW2X2uo5F3IrKXAO53mebB-pcFpXhDRuhIiqAHXXyHYDBfYVzgUIo0wVOQgPJy-QjmiaZeN6e-XCDmnWEPnwptGTr61_0Frjdw62nNqBKVhIlSOhsjkf7JqF_YsQfo6cRSv_F8EJCwqTUDwQFz0N6EX7Ezg==&c=KveG1NalNOS1hgPOq4HK2PI8xyPosyHPyLG1JyzVWrmYdcGWt4URgA==&ch=lAKMjbdjY9o5adQ_kg67es8JPwDVSis6jyxWz9J2dv-GNRFwP8ACnQ==]
MOOCs launched and provided professional development opportunities for thousands
 of high school teachers interested in learning the new AP Computer Science Principles
material.

During a Hangout on Air, beginning on Thursday, February 12, at 10am PST the creators
of these MOOCs; Jen Rosato from the College of St Scholastica and Jeff Gray from
 the University of Alabama, will join Karen Parker, CS4HS Program Manager, in a 
discussion about how their online materials might be used by other universities 
and organizations to bring CSP teacher professional development to communities across
the country.

Date and Time

Thursday, February 12

10 am PST

Click here to join the Hangout [http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?f=001LhKKX9E9X13uh6TW2tG0eMh5D41CW2X2uo5F3IrKXAO53mebB-pcFpXhDRuhIiqAXZqjnGXQjbouVzKxCghRP_zrE0th3aJ98DTpnVIcpGVTWkZwZFjhZhkaI-AJ3roA2PDvHXcTN7GDVsvtHoF9rm3jzlNt6uz2fzTjxGlV_4NDVHVcpy2Q3cjuHD6vguNbPKpsgA8wog_cY6cQQ5zL4ZhuYDDDMG38MexeNwGg5qg=&c=KveG1NalNOS1hgPOq4HK2PI8xyPosyHPyLG1JyzVWrmYdcGWt4URgA==&ch=lAKMjbdjY9o5adQ_kg67es8JPwDVSis6jyxWz9J2dv-GNRFwP8ACnQ==]

Hi Computer,

Did you know that it's easy to get more space for your Dropbox?

Upgrade your Dropbox[1]

When you upgrade your Dropbox, you can:

 - Put everything in Dropbox  with 1 TB (1,000 GB) of space for your photos, videos, docs, and other files
 - Protect the stuff you share  by adding passwords and expirations to shared links
 - Simplify collaboration  with view-only permissions for shared folders
 - Keep your stuff safe  with remote wipe for lost devices


Happy Dropboxing!
- The Dropbox Team

Mosunmade,

It does not appear that we have received your official transcript from Ladoke Akintola University of Technology yet.  You may scan and email an unofficial copy of your transcript if you have one in your possession.  You may also send  your statement of result by email to our office.  Submission of your unofficial transcript is sufficient for the application review process, but if you are selected for admission you will be required to submit your official transcript to our office.

Please know that we will process your application by your departmental deadline, and you can follow the status of your application by logging into your student portal at http://www.applyweb.com/cgi-bin/ustat.

Dear Mosunmade,

Thank you for submitting your application to the Computer Science, M.S. program at the University of Oklahoma. The Office of Graduate Admissions cannot review your application at this time since you failed to upload a transcript from your last degree-granting institution.

In order for your application to move forward in the review process, please reply to this email as soon as possible and attach a scanned copy of your transcript, mark-sheets and/or degree certificate (if applicable).

To check the status of your application and documents throughout the review process, please log into your student portal<http://messages.collegenet.com/r/c/t7vBGBRLkY-VsN4jbz5CeQ?i=9768814>. You will use the same email address and password used to create your application.

Failure to submit the required transcript in a timely manner will delay the review process for your Fall 2015 application.

Kind Regards,
Office of Graduate Admissions | University of Oklahoma
731 Elm Ave., room 318 | Norman, OK 73019
Ph: 405-325-6765 | Fx: 405-325-5345

From announcements at csta-hq.org  Thu Feb 19 13:05:17 2015
From: announcements at csta-hq.org (CSTA Announcements)
Date: Thu, 19 Feb 2015 08:05:17 -0500
Subject: [Cs] 2015 Annual Conference Registration Is Now Open
Message-ID: <1120141884001.1109536700669.4523.0.290803JL.1002@scheduler.constantcontact.com>

~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~
~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~

Bigger and Better than Ever!

2015 CSTA Annual Conference
July 12-14, 2015, at the Hilton DFW Lakes, Grapevine, Texas

Registration is now open for the CSTA annual conference. CSTA 2015 is a professional
development opportunity for computer science and information technology teachers
 who need practical, classroom-focused information to help them prepare their students
for the future. Conference content is peer reviewed and peer or industry led, making
it relevant to today's classroom needs. This year we are staying true to being "bigger
and better than ever" so we have expanded our conference to span three days, with
two days worth of workshops, more exhibitors, along with multiple networking opportunities.

Highlights:


* Explore issues and trends relating directly to your classroom
* Learn, network and interact
* Choose from various workshops and breakout sessions
* Amazing value (complimentary conference Wi-Fi, breakfast, lunch and snacks - CHECK!)
at approximately $100/day!

Some of this year's session topics include:


* Advanced Placement Computer Science
* Computational Thinking
* Increasing Enrollment in Computer Science
* Programming
* Robotics

Keynotes:


* Megan Smith, Chief Technology Officer of the United States - Invited
* Randy Pitchford, Aaron Thibault and Jimmy Sieben with Gearbox [http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?f=001_3SWd6pjQKG7fsJdmLMPqeP4uZs8G6iWgPoLo1w-foQjWmMag-Y12Q8i2umLJSJjZpROPCPPMo0H89tgkmb99BYFx_f8tpoaX6kdHlQwfvDquKNGx5maGlMEC4Fdb9BDqBEl5zILcEE19HqD03-okMMc3sHp6m3uBqyMU7sFrXc=&c=m7oxv8Ilj--ec5DP3A6vcpHZcweP0yyo6ltaUmFCahB0VPGAZyn4pw==&ch=dhSypp-2X5_6P_FdioouwuCXy86twefag9hwafCqo4JsZbCoR0mALw==]

Pre-registration is required and will be accepted for the first 500 teachers. The
registration deadline is June 26, 2015. Also, please note that you must complete
 the payment portion of the online form in order to be fully registered for the 
conference!

As always, we thank our sponsors for their generous donations. Your registration
 fee will include networking opportunities, lunch and resource materials. The 2015
CSTA Annual Conference is made possible by the generous support of Google, Lockheed
Martin, Oracle Academy and the University of Texas at Dallas.

Costs:

Conference registration (which includes a community session on Sunday (July 12) 
afternoon, Monday night's event with the University of Texas at Dallas, and all 
general and plenary sessions on Tuesday (July 14) is $100 if you register by April
15. From April 16-June 26 the price is $150, and after that the price increases 
to $225.

Workshops are a separate price, and this year we have expanded our offerings to 
include options on Sunday, as well as Monday. The price for workshops is $100 for
the first one, and $50 for each additional workshop (maximum number of three).

Please note that all workshops are "bring your own laptop" and that workshop registration
is limited to 30-40 participants; so be sure to register early to get your workshop
choice. As an additional reminder, we DO NOT accept workshop registrations onsite,
and there is NO switching of options.

Message-ID: <D1D89E6CDFA0974EAAECE0300257B1B30148E1158F42@EXCH-MBX27.allegisgroup.com>

Hi,

I am a project manager and business analyst recruiter at TEKsystems in Oklahoma City. TEKsystems is the #1 IT Staffing and Services company in the nation. We rarely work at staffing junior level positions, though we have recently acquired the need for 2 junior level business analysts. We are hoping to find 2 students who have either graduated recently or are graduating this May in Computer Science and who are eager to learn and advance their career. They would be working officially as "business analysts" or "business systems analysts" for Mercury Insurance in Oklahoma City. The pay would be ~$15/hour for a 6 month 40 hour/week contract. It's a great way to start building a career in the IT community now, great pay, and a good way to build up the resume early.

If there is anyone in particular I should speak to, please forward my information along to the respective party.

From icnc-fskd-cfp at hnu.edu.cn  Mon Feb 23 23:37:18 2015
From: icnc-fskd-cfp at hnu.edu.cn (Prof Li)
Date: Tue, 24 Feb 2015 07:37:18 +0800
Subject: [Cs] ICNC-FSKD 2015 Submissions Extended 15 March: Submitting to
	IEEE Xplore/EI Compendex/ISI 2015/2/24 7:37:31 bq5jkjfw
Message-ID: <20150224073731062456@hnu.edu.cn>

Dear Colleague,
 
We cordially invite you to submit a paper to the upcoming 2015 11th International Conference on Natural Computation (ICNC 2015) and 2015 12th International Conference on Fuzzy Systems and Knowledge Discovery (FSKD 2015), to be jointly held from 15-17 August 2015 in Zhangjiajie, China. Due to numerous requests, the submission deadline is extended to 15 March 2015.
 
Zhangjiajie is a city in the northwestern part of Hunan province. Nearby is the Wulingyuan Scenic Area, a UNESCO World Heritage Site and an AAAAA (the highest class) scenic area in China. Towering sandstones mesas, dense forests, and deep ravines form the gorgeous and mysterious natural landscape. With many spectacularly-shaped stone pillars, hidden valleys, seas of cloud, majestic waterfalls, wandering streams, clear lakes, and limestone caves, Wulingyuan is a must-see in China. Avatar, James Cameron?s block-buster movie, did much of its filming in these beautiful mountains.  
 
As with the past ICNC-FSKD conferences, all papers in conference proceedings will be submitted to both EI Compendex and ISTP (ISI Proceedings), as well as IEEE Xplore (all previous ICNC-FSKD conferences from 2005 to 2013 have been indexed in Ei Compendex). Extended versions of selected best papers will appear in an ICNC-FSKD special issue of International Journal of Pattern Recognition and Artificial Intelligence, a SCI-index journal. ICNC-FSKD 2015 is technically co-sponsored by the IEEE Circuits and Systems Society (pending).
 
ICNC-FSKD is a premier international forum for scientists and researchers to present the state of the art of data mining and intelligent methods inspired from nature, particularly biological, linguistic, and physical systems, with applications to computers, circuits, systems, control, robotics, communications, and more. This is an exciting and emerging interdisciplinary area in which a wide range of theory and methodologies are being investigated and developed to tackle complex and challenging problems. The registration fee of US-D410 includes proceedings, lunches, dinners, banquet, coffee breaks, and all technical sessions.
 
To promote international participation of researchers from outside the country/region where the conference is held (i.e., China?s mainland), researchers outside of China?s mainland are encouraged to propose invited sessions. An honorarium of US-D400 will be enjoyed by the organizer(s) for each completed (with at least 6 registered papers) invited session. The first author of each paper in an invited session must not be affiliated with an organization in China?s mainland. "(Invited Paper)" may be added below the title of each paper in the invited sessions. Invited session organizers will solicit submissions, conduct reviews and recommend accept/reject decisions on the submitted papers. Invited session organizers will be able to set their own submission and review schedules, as long as a set of recommended papers is determined by 3 June 2015. Each invited session proposal should include: (1) the name, bio, and contact information of each organizer of the invited session; (2) the title and a short synopsis of the invited session. Please send your proposal to icnc-fskd at hnu.edu.cn
 
For more information, visit the conference web page:
 
   http://icnc-fskd.hnu.edu.cn/
 
If you have any questions after visiting the conference web page, please email the secretariat at icnc-fskd at hnu.edu.cn
 
Join us at this major event in beautiful Zhangjiajie !!!
 
Organizing Committee
icnc-fskd at hnu.edu.cn
 
P.S.: Kindly forward to your colleagues and students in your school/department.
 
If you wish to unsubscribe, in which case we apologize, please reply with " unsubscribe  cs at ou.edu " in your email subject. Thanks.
 
 
2015/2/24 7:37:31 g9smu

CSTA Announcements

URLsml [http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?f=001gE7LkXLkQlTbhn5WL3rVvK7_4NX7VFQQ9V5W-JOOgYFPyBV41Vs4oZevrpMBTVtiykf4Dv9PylhaMPqd5bY400QA13QRWClNN3QEOQ-clnY5jJdYv0TQx9_yTnVMBMLMWTPZbrQ89hgacbT1_HYuF17vVog5XigSwDesYtoSqf8=&c=Tl-YwKd61xmpTH9wP7B-HdVqdeNJyw4G3vR_Hma7BUC43nI8s7mFPA==&ch=kkluj_WFC6LTZJ3sNVosUVR_WAJChC1W8deM-bQdvjaQqex8aZI02g==]

Hi, just a reminder that you're receiving this email because you have expressed 
an interest in CSTA. Don't forget to add announcements at csta-hq.org to your address
book so we'll be sure to land in your inbox!

Lockheed Martin Hosts Code Quest Computer Programming Competition

Lockheed Martin is committed to inspiring students to pursue future careers in science,
technology, engineering and math (STEM).  On April 18, 2015, Lockheed Martin will
host Code Quest, a computer programming competition consisting of 15-20 questions
created by Lockheed Martin IT professionals. The competition welcomes high school
students, in teams of two to three, from across the U.S. to compete in a rigorous,
2.5 hour, problem set.

Code Quest provides students the opportunity to test their computer coding knowledge
and encourages them to pursue studies in STEM. The competition also provides students
an in-depth look at the Lockheed Martin facilities and future career opportunities.

*Code Quest will be held in the following locations:

Denver, Colorado

Fort Worth, Texas

Marietta, Georgia

Orlando, Florida

Owego, New York

Sunnyvale, California

Washington D.C. Metro

*Space is limited and registration is on a first-come, first-served basis for all
eligible teams.

To register a team online, visit the Code Quest website. [http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?f=001gE7LkXLkQlTbhn5WL3rVvK7_4NX7VFQQ9V5W-JOOgYFPyBV41Vs4oQBLtIWzsWpgcGV--2k5sch6yo8B641wTuYhJwVd2SMXgR2QtD1MI2o9q9RSjfe6WVt1ptyWoeq95t9qfxx5WmvCsTxtyaTIarGeHDXgD7Njww2AntWov0Ln19ekNspFvzPrxjK8uxnHbC8-c1N34nydUY0HOhwn73DJCK2IS19De6vW6vYJbxTSDK9x3T9LUcAYY3turEiq&c=Tl-YwKd61xmpTH9wP7B-HdVqdeNJyw4G3vR_Hma7BUC43nI8s7mFPA==&ch=kkluj_WFC6LTZJ3sNVosUVR_WAJChC1W8deM-bQdvjaQqex8aZI02g==]
For more information, contact Diana Truss at diana.m.truss at lmco.com [mailto:diana.m.truss at lmco.com]
or 817-763-7970.

From customerservice at csta-hq.org  Thu Mar  5 19:12:06 2015
From: customerservice at csta-hq.org (Lindsay Bradley)

Subject: [Cs] Your CSTA Institutional Membership
Message-ID: <CAN+xDtYO+2qXznT3mDrZ+GkiWmxXCGkG3OF-bAF6QvH8C0BoTg@mail.gmail.com>

Dear CSTA Member,

CSTA has been working hard to build a strong community of educators
dedicated to addressing serious issues in K-12 computer science education.
As an institutional member of this organization, you can access key
resources that will help you reach more teachers and increase the
effectiveness of your K-12 outreach programs.

CSTA is the premier K-12 computer science education organization with
direct access to more than 19,000 computer science educators. *As a CSTA
institutional member, you have access to these members through the
following channels:*

   - Directed email blasts to CSTA members concerning your K-12 outreach
   events
   - Help locating CS teachers in your area
   - Free event notices on the CSTA Announcements web page
   - Free link from our Members Making a Difference web page
   - An article featuring your program in the CSTA *Voice*
   - Free materials on careers in computing, such as posters and brochures,
   for your outreach events
   - Preferred access to key professional development opportunities

*CSTA also provides additional benefits designed specifically for
institutional members. These include:*

   - Free copies of curriculum documents
   - Free copies of white papers and advocacy resources
   - Subscription to the CSTA *Voice *e-newsletter
   - Access to cutting edge research and analysis on current trends in K-12
   computing education
   - Subscription to *The Connector*, a quarterly e-newsletter specifically
   designed for Institutional members.

By renewing your CSTA membership (1-year $200 or 2-year $380) you will
continue to receive the member benefits that help keep you in touch with
computer science teachers.

*Renewing your CSTA membership keeps you in touch with K-12. *Simply fax
your renewal to +1-212-944-1318 or send to ACM/CSTA, P.O. Box 30778, NY, NY
10117-3509

Yours truly,

Lindsay Bradley
Project Coordinator
Computer Science Teachers Association (CSTA)
(541) 829-1272
customerservice at csta-hq.org

From icnc-fskd-cfp at hnu.edu.cn  Sun Mar  8 01:47:26 2015
From: icnc-fskd-cfp at hnu.edu.cn (Prof Li)
Date: Sun, 8 Mar 2015 09:47:26 +0800
Subject: [Cs] ICNC-FSKD 2015 Submissions Extended 15 March: Submitting to
	IEEE Xplore/EI Compendex/ISI 2015/3/8 9:47:38 lkfk
Message-ID: <20150308094738327405@hnu.edu.cn>

Dear Colleague,
 
We cordially invite you to submit a paper to the upcoming 2015 11th International Conference on Natural Computation (ICNC 2015) and 2015 12th International Conference on Fuzzy Systems and Knowledge Discovery (FSKD 2015), to be jointly held from 15-17 August 2015 in Zhangjiajie, China. Due to numerous requests, the submission deadline is extended to 15 March 2015.
 
Zhangjiajie is a city in the northwestern part of Hunan province. Nearby is the Wulingyuan Scenic Area, a UNESCO World Heritage Site and an AAAAA (the highest class) scenic area in China. Towering sandstones mesas, dense forests, and deep ravines form the gorgeous and mysterious natural landscape. With many spectacularly-shaped stone pillars, hidden valleys, seas of cloud, majestic waterfalls, wandering streams, clear lakes, and limestone caves, Wulingyuan is a must-see in China. Avatar, James Cameron?s block-buster movie, did much of its filming in these beautiful mountains.  
 
As with the past ICNC-FSKD conferences, all papers in conference proceedings will be submitted to both EI Compendex and ISTP (ISI Proceedings), as well as IEEE Xplore (all previous ICNC-FSKD conferences from 2005 to 2013 have been indexed in Ei Compendex). Extended versions of selected best papers will appear in an ICNC-FSKD special issue of International Journal of Pattern Recognition and Artificial Intelligence, a SCI-index journal. ICNC-FSKD 2015 is technically co-sponsored by the IEEE Circuits and Systems Society (pending).
 
ICNC-FSKD is a premier international forum for scientists and researchers to present the state of the art of data mining and intelligent methods inspired from nature, particularly biological, linguistic, and physical systems, with applications to computers, circuits, systems, control, robotics, communications, and more. This is an exciting and emerging interdisciplinary area in which a wide range of theory and methodologies are being investigated and developed to tackle complex and challenging problems. The registration fee of US-D410 includes proceedings, lunches, dinners, banquet, coffee breaks, and all technical sessions.
 
To promote international participation of researchers from outside the country/region where the conference is held (i.e., China?s mainland), researchers outside of China?s mainland are encouraged to propose invited sessions. An honorarium of US-D400 will be enjoyed by the organizer(s) for each completed (with at least 6 registered papers) invited session. The first author of each paper in an invited session must not be affiliated with an organization in China?s mainland. "(Invited Paper)" may be added below the title of each paper in the invited sessions. Invited session organizers will solicit submissions, conduct reviews and recommend accept/reject decisions on the submitted papers. Invited session organizers will be able to set their own submission and review schedules, as long as a set of recommended papers is determined by 3 June 2015. Each invited session proposal should include: (1) the name, bio, and contact information of each organizer of the invited session; (2) the title and a short synopsis of the invited session. Please send your proposal to icnc-fskd at hnu.edu.cn
 
For more information, visit the conference web page:
 
   http://icnc-fskd.hnu.edu.cn/
 
If you have any questions after visiting the conference web page, please email the secretariat at icnc-fskd at hnu.edu.cn
 
Join us at this major event in beautiful Zhangjiajie !!!
 
Organizing Committee
icnc-fskd at hnu.edu.cn
 
P.S.: Kindly forward to your colleagues and students in your school/department.
 
If you wish to unsubscribe, in which case we apologize, please reply with " unsubscribe  cs at ou.edu " in your email subject. Thanks.
 
 
2015/3/8 9:47:38 jyzyyp

From georgio at fit.edu  Wed Mar 11 11:03:43 2015
From: georgio at fit.edu (Georgios  Anagnostopoulos)
Date: Wed, 11 Mar 2015 11:03:43 +0000
Subject: [Cs] REU summer internship in Machine Learning - apply by 31 March
 2015 [kindly forward]
Message-ID: <EF1B06A588B7A1489617DE4EDC5E6A8BD14E4A32@EX10-BE1.fit.edu>

Dear Prof. Gruenwald,



Below you will find an announcement for an NSF Research Experiences for Undergraduates (REU) program offered this summer. I would be very grateful, if you could forward it to the undergraduate students in your department, as you did last year (for which I am obliged to you).



Regards,



Dr. Georgios C. Anagnostopoulos

Director, The AMALTHEA REU Program

Associate Professor, ECE Dept.

Florida Institute of Technology

Melbourne, Florida

Email: georgio at fit.edu<mailto:georgio at fit.edu>

URL:   http://my.fit.edu/~georgio









=== THE 2015 AMALTHEA REU PROGRAM ===





AN OPPORTUNITY FOR A 10-WEEK RESEARCH EXPERIENCE FOR UNDERGRADUATE STUDENTS is available in the area of Machine Learning. The program is sponsored by the National Science Foundation and is offered by the Information Characterization & Exploitation (ICE) Laboratory at Florida Institute of Technology (FIT) in Melbourne, Florida.



Machine Learning (ML) gradually evolved as a branch of Artificial Intelligence with its theory and applications positioned at the juncture of Computer Science, Engineering, Mathematics, Statistics and, even, Physics. Nowadays, ML's role in successfully addressing hard, real-world technological challenges has become ever more current and central. Moreover, its presence and importance now permeates several aspects not only of cutting-edge technology such as computer vision, stock market prediction and big data analytics, but also our daily life through voice-driven searches on our smart phones or movie recommendations on video streaming services to name only a few.



The program currently accepts applications in order to form a very diverse, multi-disciplinary cohort of nascent researchers for this summer. Minorities, women and people with disabilities are especially encouraged to apply.



ELIGIBILITY

Without exceptions, applicants must be:

=> Majoring in an Engineering or Science discipline

=> US citizens or permanent residents

=> Undergraduates in good academic standing



BENEFITS

=> Exposure to the exciting world of Machine Learning and its applications

=> Participate in a one-week crash course to familiarize yourself with Machine Learning

=> Work with experienced student mentors and experts in the field

=> Participate and contribute to cutting-edge Machine Learning research

=> Take part in visits to our local industry

=> Paid travel and accommodation expenses

=> Receive a competitive stipend for per diem expenses

=> Visit Central Florida venues such as Disney attractions and NASA's Kennedy Space Center

=> Meet new people

=> Make new friends



Application Deadline: March 31, 2015

Apply online: http://www.amalthea-reu.org



For more information, visit our Web site at www.amalthea-reu.org or contact:



Dr. Georgios C. Anagnostopoulos

Department of Electrical & Computer Engineering

Florida Institute of Technology

150 West University Boulevard

Melbourne, Florida 32901-6975

Phone 321-674-7125 | Fax 321-674-8192

E-mail: georgio at fit.edu<mailto:georgio at fit.edu>

iD Tech and Code.org Give 100 Girls Scholarships to Attend Summer STEM Program

iD Tech knows that the world needs more girls in STEM. This year, iD Tech is partnering
with Code.org, a non-profit dedicated to expanding participation in computer science,
to send 100 girls to iD Tech Camps for free! At this weeklong summer program, ages
7-17 create mobile apps, design video games, mod with Minecraft, build robots, code
with C++ and Java, produce movies, and more. Programs are held in 30 states nationwide.
Girls can apply for a scholarship at www.iDTech.com/girls [http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?f=001Si-Vun--WKO5amgMPuMtFOMq6J2hTlOOQ7hA4QcK0V0Ea8Vng07Y5I-07R82TsuI0V34vHB_sc_oGy0rNAmHT9iN-u--FsBjKp4MP-hng2tkGxpL6x-7vLZKkiFGE0YFGWlJwvSWIlAZR_pccufhi9ELF_APwMLL-AKtz3XhwOpdnWMad1Gnxg==&c=d2YZ70MCa5MRvoHeQfKmcKt7a2mX5V6r6Uyj9-n47lGEjiwc7md9hQ==&ch=XtxHC_jsdkXQTg2nKA5sQN2uriCt8_lQX9U5l35DBJkRT9HmAJfaGQ==]
through April 1st. To learn more about Code.org, please visit http://code.org/.

Next Roadtrip Nation to Focus on CS Education
Microsoft is teaming up with Roadtrip Nation [http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?f=001fX4--GeaVzlYfKdAU7b7AZLzjgu9KFpLfs2yUw1zrEyA_xwlhd-Zj0HXnuK9RaTuap3kEGFF4Xcf3bunN-AVY0xo1eVTVhUr4DpT113MdJUjcTPdiEgYnt3ftiOT0FoCHabXw6cDhHJRI7ReM-PAQi84WG_plgJxx9-lr51tHNN8DblcFFpz7mLjYk8nddlj-Zr8avZgDQayDB6HIXJnBkDpOR6tmTaZhkC--jJgRx3ibbNP65TRXDUTlCJ20-SxNcLYzshwrhWLG-jpqzenha0k0KVAPHeNKPsDff7wUG5Pyg4e41m3vhmBdQ4pBIAh&c=RyrVmhl4V8aIQDEvFM__WW0w_-CG0oKo1foHTg8861Wz6SVQ1feNeA==&ch=mj9aujFDKUYcUDkeICpTVE2TJWcmOIO6RPsPtpJPgHUbID0YWE5vSg==]
to send three dynamic, diverse, young people who are interested in computer science
on a four-week cross-country adventure to discover the exciting--and growing--possibilities
in the industry. The three will travel in Roadtrip Nation's Green RV, and will interview
professionals all over the country who have turned their passion for computer science
into fulfilling careers. The experience will be filmed and will appear on Roadtrip
Nation's long-running documentary series [http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?f=001fX4--GeaVzlYfKdAU7b7AZLzjgu9KFpLfs2yUw1zrEyA_xwlhd-Zj0HXnuK9RaTu9WriFXxiSGwMfOvjDw9XFxpRy7eXaGLVePjInwe1oW-gAxasGjCXySgIG4U4GUcYNhj9yXkL272vquM_DdXJ2QPxGq0z2_Wr_Dtn5GHm2FlAyuyaL7gwWqxFk_xHTz23lMWJNwJQ16Hf-hUq4EI6PbzPPrecOcJxJ_yTa2ETeHI=&c=RyrVmhl4V8aIQDEvFM__WW0w_-CG0oKo1foHTg8861Wz6SVQ1feNeA==&ch=mj9aujFDKUYcUDkeICpTVE2TJWcmOIO6RPsPtpJPgHUbID0YWE5vSg==]
and be incorporated into Roadtrip Nation's educational resources. [http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?f=001fX4--GeaVzlYfKdAU7b7AZLzjgu9KFpLfs2yUw1zrEyA_xwlhd-Zj0HXnuK9RaTu-CeiE-Ka6p4WqA6R8qubIm-d1N-iCGkRLUdRGNz3a-NkUsYyjckO_lcPEQbhETh_ZDOdXlkcMzf3YfX9qhlII-hoC_e6kFKkSkQFDDaEZoeQa8YQ4Hao1-FtzwYnY5Wb&c=RyrVmhl4V8aIQDEvFM__WW0w_-CG0oKo1foHTg8861Wz6SVQ1feNeA==&ch=mj9aujFDKUYcUDkeICpTVE2TJWcmOIO6RPsPtpJPgHUbID0YWE5vSg==]

From icdmxw at GMAIL.COM  Mon Mar 23 18:10:41 2015
From: icdmxw at GMAIL.COM (ICDM 2015)
Date: Mon, 23 Mar 2015 13:10:41 -0500
Subject: [Cs] ICDM 2015 Call for Papers
Message-ID: <CAPVPyJj+uXqLCsoCRUgQ2apVYBqVY=58TtE3HorPXJZ9b1YAbw@mail.gmail.com>

Call for Papers

ICDM '15: The 15th IEEE International Conference on Data Mining
***************************************************************

November 14-17, 2015, Atlantic City, NJ, USA
http://icdm2015.stonybrook.edu/

Important Dates
***************

All deadlines are at 11:59PM Pacific Daylight Time
* Workshop proposals:                                Mar 19, 2015
* Workshop notification:                             Mar 29, 2015
* ICDM contest proposals:                            Mar 29, 2015
* Full paper submissions:                            Jun 03, 2015
* Demo proposals:                                    Jul 13, 2015
* Workshop paper submissions:                        Jul 20, 2015
* Tutorial proposals:                                Aug 01, 2015
* Conference paper, tutorial, demo notifications:    Aug 25, 2015
* Workshop paper notifications:                      Sep 01, 2015
* Conference dates:                                  Nov 14-17, 2015

The IEEE International Conference on Data Mining series (ICDM) has
established itself as the world's premier research conference in data
mining. It provides an international forum for presentation of
original research results, as well as exchange and dissemination of
innovative, practical development experiences. The conference covers
all aspects of data mining, including algorithms, software and
systems, and applications. ICDM draws researchers and application
developers from a wide range of data mining related areas such as
statistics, machine learning, pattern recognition, databases and data
warehousing, data visualization, knowledge-based systems, and high
performance computing. By promoting novel, high quality research
findings, and innovative solutions to challenging data mining
problems, the conference seeks to continuously advance the
state-of-the-art in data mining. Besides the technical program, the
conference features workshops, tutorials, panels and, since 2007, the
ICDM data mining contest.

Topics of Interest
******************

Topics of interest include, but are not limited to:

* Foundations, algorithms, models, and theory of data mining
* Machine learning and statistical methods for data mining
* Mining text, semi-structured, spatio-temporal, streaming, graph,
  web, multimedia data
* Data mining systems and platforms, their efficiency, scalability,
  and privacy
* Data mining in modeling, visualization, personalization, and
recommendation
* Applications of data mining in all domains including social, web,
  bioinformatics, and finance

Submission Guidelines
*********************

Paper submissions should be limited to a maximum of ten (10) pages, in
the IEEE 2-column format (templates available at
http://www.ieee.org/conferences_events/conferences/publishing/templates.html
),
including the bibliography and any possible appendices. Submissions
longer than 10 pages will be rejected without a review. All
submissions will be triple-blind reviewed by the Program Committee on
the basis of technical quality, relevance to data mining, originality,
significance, and clarity. Author names and affiliations must not
appear in the submissions, and bibliographic references must be
adjusted to preserve author anonymity. Accepted papers will be
published in the conference proceedings by the IEEE Computer Society
Press.

All manuscripts are submitted as full papers and are reviewed based on
their scientific merit. There is no separate abstract submission
step. There are no separate industrial, application, short paper or
poster tracks.

Manuscripts must be submitted electronically in online submission
system (https://wi-lab.com/cyberchair/2015/icdm15/cbc_index.php). We
do not accept email submissions.

Repeatability
*************

Every effort should be made to enable the code and the datasets (or
their closest publicly available equivalents) and all relevant
parameter specifications available to reviewers and readers so that
the results can be independently replicated. While we cannot expect
*every* dataset used to be made public, it is in the best interest of
the authors to make as many as possible available (in the worst case,
a sampled or an anonymized version). To retain anonymity of
submissions, any such additional material should be anonymized as
well, and be published on an anonymous website (such as DropBox). The
repeatability factor will play an important role in the reviewer's
assessment of the submission.

Best Paper Awards
*****************

Awards will be conferred at the conference on the authors of the best
research paper, the best application paper, and the best student
paper. A selected number of accepted papers will be invited for
possible inclusion, in an expanded and revised form, in the Knowledge
and Information Systems journal published by Springer-Verlag.

Attendance
**********

ICDM is forum for presenting and discussing current research in data
mining. Therefore, at least one author of an accepted paper must
complete a regular conference registration and present the paper in
the conference, in order for the paper to be included in the
proceedings and program.

Hi, just a reminder that you're receiving this email because you have expressed 
an interest in CSTA. Don't forget to add announcements at csta-hq.org to your address

Computer Science Educators,

GG|Interactive, a fifteen-year veteran video game studio based in Vancouver, WA,
 is offering a computer science curriculum focused on digital game design and programming.
Schools can receive an unlimited number of licenses for the curriculum at no cost
but you must register at www.GGInteractive.com [http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?f=001bLFOCcncZLxsT5utFLKo8Q7GE5VDZ9ZSSx2azzoktPjmKqXHDF2TMYagqBlTG20vdkoETrKOwFNCxVgKL1XuRayTHd_57OqdQ-aUL8WEBhCH5tM37OC0Jz2pZ9TjJXor3t6_os_W8w7H4WCCc_2Guvkrlls8rn3BB6TrQs0IeKbv5AMzCfVcNw==&c=aZaawaMaR1njfBmga6kiOj9beKLQTFAPZtNbARQZsrdq-2AmGjf7Og==&ch=aimPNNEeWnRkEQnciwLw8Dcn1YO7rBCeUxXIi8SSlSV3nYBR2d1NrQ==]
by midnight, March 31st.

In 2013, the fifth largest school district in the United States asked us to help
 design a framework and standard, for teaching game design and development courses.
Once complete, we learned that schools and teachers had very few options for supporting
curriculum to teach game design or game programming courses. In response, we created
our education division.

Teachers started teaching our courses worldwide in late 2014. The curriculum includes
video lectures, assessments, exercises, and reference text; combined with a glossary,
index, and teacher guides. It is roughly 120 hours of coursework and is designed
 for the teacher with little or no computer science experience. To date, we have
 had over 500 schools and 20,000 students registered for the curriculum.

You can begin your free year immediately, or you can wait and start this coming 
fall for the 2015-16 school year, the choice is yours. Just register yourself as
 a teacher, on the site now. There is no contract or obligation to use this in the
future, although we are confident you will like what you see.

Again, this promotion ends on March 31st at midnight. You need to act quickly and
register as soon as possible. Please visit our website (www.GGInteractive.com [http://r20.rs6.net/tn.jsp?f=001bLFOCcncZLxsT5utFLKo8Q7GE5VDZ9ZSSx2azzoktPjmKqXHDF2TMYagqBlTG20vdkoETrKOwFNCxVgKL1XuRayTHd_57OqdQ-aUL8WEBhCH5tM37OC0Jz2pZ9TjJXor3t6_os_W8w7H4WCCc_2Guvkrlls8rn3BB6TrQs0IeKbv5AMzCfVcNw==&c=aZaawaMaR1njfBmga6kiOj9beKLQTFAPZtNbARQZsrdq-2AmGjf7Og==&ch=aimPNNEeWnRkEQnciwLw8Dcn1YO7rBCeUxXIi8SSlSV3nYBR2d1NrQ==])
for more information and registration.

We look forward to hearing from you, and helping you and your students learn Computer
Science in Game Design. If you have questions please email us directly at Education at gginteractive.com
[mailto:Education at gginteractive.com]

Sincerely,

The GG|Interactive Team

Education at gginteractive.com [mailto:Education at gginteractive.com]
